                        cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An advanced high-energy sodium ion full battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7/VOPO4 layered materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Hongsen; Peng, Lele; Zhu, Yue; Chen, Dahong; Zhang, Xiaogang; Yu, Guihua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In virtue of the abundant sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be one of the promising alternatives to lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, current research concs. mostly on sodium ion half-cells, and the development of sodium ion full cells with high performance remains a crit. challenge.  Here we rationally designed a full sodium-ion battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7 and VOPO4 materials as the anodes and cathodes, owing to their advantageous electrochem. features.  The full cell outputs one of the highest operating voltages close to 2.9 V and delivers a large reversible capacity of 114 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1C.  It also shows outstanding rate capability (∼74 mA h g-1 at 2C rate) and excellent cycling stability (92.4% capacity retention after 100 cycles).  A high energy d. of 220 W h kg-1 is achieved, which is comparable to the state-of-the-art LIBs.  Moreover, the temp.-dependent charge-discharge tests indicate excellent capacity retentions in a wide temp. range of -20 to 55 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoeiSHi_Z7ig7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhOoamTZvzLrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVCmsb7J&amp;md5=e38751b094eee46fa6320e8370c3026b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1039/c5ra21235a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ai, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Type of Sodium-Ion Full-Cell with a Layered NaNi<sub>0.5</sub>Ti<sub>0.5</sub>O<sub>2</sub> Cathode and a Pre-sodiated Hard Carbon Anode</span>. <i>RSC Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">106519</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">106522</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new structure of sodium-ion full-cell with a layered NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 cathode and a pre-sodiated hard carbon anode is reported.  The pre-sodiation of the hard carbon anode, achieved via a facile approach in a three-electrode battery, can significantly enhance the initial coulombic efficiency of the sodium-ion full-cell.  As a consequence, a much higher capacity is obtained in the hard carbon/NaNi0.5Ti0.5O2 sodium-ion battery.  Based on the cathode mass, the full-cell with the pre-sodiated hard carbon anode can exhibit a reversible capacity of 93 mA h g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr_2zWMBOTW5rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhOoamTZvzLrw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWlu7rP&amp;md5=c164a42f421e9fbb6ae1ccf5d88b7dca</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600659"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard Carbon Microtubes Made from Renewable Cotton as High-Performance Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ruthenium-Oxide-Coated Sodium Vanadium Fluorophosphate Nanowires as High-Power Cathode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Manhua; Li, Biao; Yan, Huijun; Zhang, Dongtang; Wang, Xiayan; Xia, Dingguo; Guo, Guangsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">54</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6452-6456</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1433-7851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a very promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries because of their reliance on an abundant supply of sodium salts, environmental benignity, and low cost.  However, the low rate capability and poor long-term stability still hinder their practical application.  A cathode material, formed of RuO2-coated Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanowires, has a 50 nm diam. with the space group of I4/mmm.  When used as a cathode material for Na-ion batteries, a reversible capacity of 120 mAh g-1 at 1 C and 95 mAh g-1 at 20 C can be achieved after 1000 charge-discharge cycles.  The ultrahigh rate capability and enhanced cycling stability are comparable with high performance lithium cathodes.  Combining first principles computational investigation with exptl. observations, the excellent performance can be attributed to the uniform and highly conductive RuO2 coating and the preferred growth of the (002) plane in the Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanowires.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqy8Uys_JBRc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-HWa2nTyGDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmt1Sgtrw%253D&amp;md5=387cfec2625d5a109f637ff63f2938f1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/c7ee00524e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Design Strategies and Research Progress for Room-temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrolyte design strategies and research progress for room-temperature sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Che, Haiying; Chen, Suli; Xie, Yingying; Wang, Hong; Amine, Khalil; Liao, Xiao-Zhen; Ma, Zi-Feng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1075-1101</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrolyte design or functional development is very effective at promoting the performance of sodium-ion batteries, which are attractive for electrochem. energy storage devices due to abundant sodium resources and low cost.  This review discusses recent advances on electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries and comprehensive electrolyte design strategies for various materials systems as well as functional applications.  The discussion is divided into three electrolyte types: liq., solid state, and gel state.  Liq. electrolytes are further divided into different solvent types, including org. carbonate ester, ether, ionic liq., and water.  Solid-state electrolytes also contain two types: solid polymer and glass-ceramic composite.  The challenges and prospects of electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries are discussed as well.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-Z8E8XTZlgrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh-HWa2nTyGDg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmt1KjsL8%253D&amp;md5=54b8998fadfbe23f9c468a27d070afe7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201701768"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, J. (PVA) copolymer by the casting method.  Effect of the montmorillonite on ionic cond. and electrochem. properties of the polymer electrolyte was demonstrated.  The result CSPE obtained a higher ionic cond. up to 4.31 × 10-4 S cm-1 at room temp. when 4.0% MMT was contained, and the max. Li ions transference no. of 0.40 was achieved.  Electrochem. performance of the polymer solid electrolyte was evaluated in Li/polymer electrolyte/LiFePO4 coin cell.  Good performance with low capacity fading on charge-discharge cycling was achieved, indicating the potential application of the as-prepd. CSPE in Li ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrf9sJW9j3kx7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljylGwnCHOOKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhvFWktL%252FL&amp;md5=7e638e58cbac0fbe6daaa35549378fad</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201700322"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, K.-C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xing, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.-P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An in situ-Fabricated Composite Polymer Electrolyte Containing Large-Anion Lithium Salt for All-Solid-State LiFePO<sub>4</sub>/Li Batteries</span>. <i>ChemElectroChem</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>4</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2293</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2299</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we propose an in situ hydrolytic method to synthesize SiO2 nanoparticles, which are incorporated in poly(ethylene oxide)-based polymer in the presence of lithium salt with a large anion (lithium bis(oxalate) borate).  When evaluated as the solid electrolyte for electrochem. performance in lithium batteries, the as-prepd. composite polymer electrolyte (CPE) exhibits an exciting ion cond. of 1.9 mS/cm at 80 °C.  Moreover, the CPE shows a decent Li+ transference no. up to 0.69 and wide electrochem. window of 5.05 V at 60 °C.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-ion BAB triblock copolymers as highly efficient electrolytes for lithium-metal batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bouchet, Renaud; Maria, Sebastien; Meziane, Rachid; Aboulaich, Abdelmaula; Lienafa, Livie; Bonnet, Jean-Pierre; Phan, Trang N.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. energy storage is one of the main societal challenges of this century.  The performances of classical lithium-ion technol. based on liq. electrolytes have made great advances in the past two decades, but the intrinsic instability of liq. electrolytes results in safety issues.  Solid polymer electrolytes would be a perfect soln. to those safety issues, miniaturization and enhancement of energy d.  However, as in liqs., the fraction of charge carried by lithium ions is small (&lt;20%), limiting the power performances.  Solid polymer electrolytes operate at 80 °C, resulting in poor mech. properties and a limited electrochem. stability window.  Here we describe a multifunctional single-ion polymer electrolyte based on polyanionic block copolymers comprising polystyrene segments.  It overcomes most of the above limitations, with a lithium-ion transport no. close to unity, excellent mech. properties and an electrochem. stability window spanning 5 V vs. Li+/Li.  A prototype battery using this polyelectrolyte outperforms a conventional battery based on a polymer electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo5XToOi_lGi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljylGwnCHOOKw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXkvFOqsrc%253D&amp;md5=768f99531ec58f1d28eaa5a43b2f80f8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201300654"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kambe, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Archer, L.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Quasi-Solid-State Rechargeable Lithium-Ion Batteries with a Calix[4]quinone Cathode and Gel Polymer Electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Weiwei; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Wang, Lijiang; Wang, Shiwen; Li, Hao; Tao, Zhanliang; Shi, Jifu; Guan, Lunhui; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A sodium ion conducting gel polymer electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A sodium ion conducting gel polymer electrolyte based on poly(vinylidene difluoride-co-hexafluoropropylene) porous membrane is reported, which is prepd. through a simple phase sepn. process.  It exhibits high safety, good mech. properties and good electrochem. stability.  The gel polymer electrolyte provides the sodium ionic cond. of 0.60 mS cm- 1 at ambient temp., while the com. separator (Celgard 2730) offers only 0.16 mS cm- 1.  The temp. dependence of the ionic cond. from 25 to 75 °C is consistent with an Arrhenius-behavior.  The ionic transference no. of sodium ion (t+Na) in the gel polymer electrolyte is 0.30, higher than that (0.17) in the com. separator.  This provides a new direction to improve the safety of sodium ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoNS7nWYbpDH7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lix29LyOq6M0g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvF2ksLfP&amp;md5=1f1b0713f2c64850f0cc4ed39c62e1db</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.eurpolymj.2006.02.006"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stephan, A.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The composite polymer electrolyte (CPE) membranes, comprising of poly(vinylidene fluoride-hexafluoropropylene) (PVdF-HFP), aluminum oxyhydroxide, (AlO[OH]n) of two different particle sizes 7 μm/14 nm and LiN(CF3SO2)2 as lithium salt were prepd. using soln. casting technique. Also LiCr0.01Mn1.99O4/CPE/Li cells were assembled and their charge-discharge profiles were made at 70 °C.                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible P-Doped Carbon Cloth: Vacuum-Sealed Preparation and Enhanced Na-Storage Properties as Binder-Free Anode for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lu, Hong-Yan; Zhang, Xiao-Hua; Wan, Fang; Liu, Dao-Sheng; Fan, Chao-Ying; Xu, Huan-Mei; Wang, Guang; Wu, Xing-Long</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, a flexible and self-supporting P-doped carbon cloth (FPCC), which is composed of interwoven mesh of hollow microtubules with porous carbon walls, is prepd. via a vacuum-sealed doping technol. by employing the com. available cotton cloth as sustainable and scalable raw material.  When directly used as binder-free anode for sodium-ion batteries, the as-prepd. FPCC delivers superior Na-storage properties in terms of specific capacity up to 242.4 mA h g-1, high initial Coulombic efficiency of ∼72%, excellent rate capabilities (e.g., 123.1 mA h g-1 at a high current of 1 A g-1), and long-term cycle life (e.g., ∼88% capacity retention after even 600 cycles).  All these electrochem. data are better than the undoped carbon cloth control, demonstrating the significance of P-doping to enhance the Na-storage properties of cotton-derived carbon anode.  Furthermore, the technologies of electrochem. impedance spectroscopy and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique are implemented to disclose the decrease of charge transfer resistance and improvement of Na-migration kinetics, resp.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoaUBjp9ZcdJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lix29LyOq6M0g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvVyhtbc%253D&amp;md5=9aa093ebe535007ce000c30ea0086111</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2011.02.119"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Kinetic Analysis on LiFePO<sub>4</sub> Thin Films by CV, GITT, and EIS</span>. <i>Electrochim.         </div><div class="casAbstract">LiFePO4 thin films were deposited on Ti substrates by pulsed laser deposition (PLD).  The apparent chem. diffusion coeffs. of Li in the films, D~Li, were measured by cyclic voltammetry (CV), galvanostatic intermittent titrn. technique (GITT), and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy (EIS).  The av. D~Li values calcd. from CV results were in the order of 10-14 cm2 s-1.  The D~Li values obtained by GITT, and EIS techniques were at 10-14-10-18 cm2 s-1, 10-14-10-18 cm2 s-1, resp. However, the overpotential values of the LiFePO4 thin film electrodes obtained from the GITT results and the diffusion impedance deduced from the impedance spectra also show the min. values at x ∼ 0.5 for Li1-xFePO4.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Crystal structure of a new sodium vanadyl(IV) fluoride phosphate Na3{V2O2F[PO4]2}</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Massa, Werner; Yakubovich, Olga V.; Dimitrova, Olga V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Solid State Sciences</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The title compd. was prepd. by hydrothermal synthesis and its crystal structure was detd. by single crystal x-ray diffraction in the space group I4/mmm.  The crystal structure of Na3{V2O2F[PO4]2} is formed by layers of alternating [VO5F] octahedra and [PO4] tetrahedra sharing O vertexes parallel to the ab plane.  Along the c direction the V octahedra are joined pairwise through common F vertexes in the inversion centers.  The 6th O vertex of the V octahedron is the terminal oxo ligand of a vanadyl group.  Thus, the structure is described by a mixed paraframework of octahedra and tetrahedra {V2O2F[PO4]2}∞∞∞ with disordered Na atoms in the interstices.  The new phase is discussed as a member in the row of compds. structurally related to the mineral natisite and VOPO4·2H2O.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGriN7GlWAge_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBVyQX08vhtg"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A High-Capacity, Low-Cost Layered Sodium Manganese Oxide Material as Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Guo, Shaohua; Yu, Haijun; Jian, Zelang; Liu, Pan; Zhu, Yanbei; Guo, Xianwei; Chen, Mingwei; Ishida, Masayoshi; Zhou, Haoshen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemSusChem</span>

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrochemically driven phase transitions in insertion electrodes for lithium-ion batteries: examples in lithium metal phosphate olivines</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tang, Ming; Carter, W.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The thermodn. and kinetics of phase transformations in electrochem. systems are reviewed.  Phase transitions in LiMPO4 (M = Fe, Mn, Ni, Co) olivines are highlighted.  The phase transformation phenomena in LiMPO4 are diverse and include thermodn. effects of particle size and applied overpotential, the appearance of metastable phases, and the effects of defects from at. disorder and aliovalent doping.  Such phenomena also include kinetic effects such as interface motion and diffusion of Li-electron complexes.  The nature of phase transitions directly influences electrode performance in battery applications.  Reduced particle size and doping can reduce or eliminate room-temp. Li miscibility gaps, which in turn affect characteristics of state of charge vs. voltage and the elastic energy due to vol. mismatches between phases.  Near the conditions for a phase transition, Li diffusion coeffs. are reduced.  Nucleation and growth kinetics produce a series of phase transition sequences, which can result in the accumulation of noncryst. phases during electrochem. cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoxOB__opnJ67Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljBVyQX08vhtg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtVClt7bI&amp;md5=e578f53bfd9ddc26ed7b8112228b920e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1007/s10008-013-2342-6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Böckenfeld, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Balducci, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Determination of Sodium Ion Diffusion Coefficients in Sodium Vanadium Phosphate</span>. <i>J.         (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A polymer system based on oligo (ethylene glycol) Me ether methacrylate (OEGMA) and cyclic carbonate methacrylate (CCMA) was chosen as matrix to realize high-performance gel polymer electrolytes due to the fact that both monomers are able to interact with the liq. electrolyte, thus, retaining it inside the matrix.  Addnl., OEGMA enables high flexibility, while CCMA provides mech. stability.  The polymer displays a high thermal stability up to 200 °C and a glass transition temp. below room temp. (5 °C) allowing an easy handling of the obtained films.  By immobilizing the liq. electrolyte 1 M LiPF6 in EC:DMC 1:1 w:w in the polymer host a gel polymer electrolyte with a high cond. of 2.3 mS cm-1 at 25 °C and a stable cycling behavior with high capacities and efficiencies in Li(Ni1/3Co1/3Mn1/3)O2 (NCM)/graphite full cells is obtained.  The investigated gel polymer electrolyte is identified as promising electrolyte for lithium-ion batteries, because it combines good electrochem. properties comparable to that of liq. electrolytes with the safety advantage that no leakage of the flammable electrolyte solvents can occur.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpDMmqJwdtDI7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuQbfCid4Opg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtlagsrvF&amp;md5=2a9ab468f9aa45cc4b912c4ad1798249</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/c7ta04886f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, S.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jan, J.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, Y.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Teng, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Diode-Like Gel Polymer Electrolytes for Full-Cell Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">17476</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">17481</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c7ta04886f</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D17476-17481%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DY.-Y.%2BLin%26author%3DY.-M.%2BChen%26author%3DS.-S.%2BHou%26author%3DJ.-S.%2BJan%26author%3DY.-L.%2BLee%26author%3DH.%2BTeng%26title%3DDiode-Like%2BGel%2BPolymer%2BElectrolytes%2Bfor%2BFull-Cell%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc7ta04886f&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b02768&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc7ta04886f&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Diode-like gel polymer electrolytes for full-cell lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Yong-Yi; Chen, Yen-Ming; Hou, Sheng-Shu; Jan, Jeng-Shiung; Lee, Yuh-Lang; Teng, Hsisheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">33</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">17476-17481</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This study designs a pos.-intrinsic-neg. (PIN)-diode-like gel polymer electrolyte (GPE) for a full-cell graphite|electrolyte|LiFePO4 Li ion battery to facilitate interfacial ion transfer at both the anode and cathode.  The diode-like GPE comprises an intrinsic poly(acrylonitrile-co-methyl-acrylate)-hosted electrolyte layer, as well as pos. and neg. layers that are synthesized by doping the intrinsic layer with TiO2 and SiO2 nanoparticles, which resp. exhibits pos. and neg. zeta potentials.  The pos. layer that adsorbs PF6- anions is in contact with the LiFePO4 cathode of the battery to facilitate the transfer of Li+ cations across the interface.  The neg. layer, which is in contact with the graphite anode, adsorbs Li+ cations to suppress accumulation and prevent the intercalation of solvated Li+ into the graphitic framework.  The intrinsic layer acts as a neutralization zone to lower the current-rectification effect of the p-n junction.  This PIN-configuration design for electrolytes enhances the ultimate capacity of the full-cell battery, exhibits high rate capacity retention, and increases the lifespan (87% capacity retained after 500 charge-discharge cycles).</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqG-x_HB9gwfLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuQbfCid4Opg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1ektr3L&amp;md5=2e409c98b75b6a0b3e8d64cd3d0c7b0f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref47'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.5b05179"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Di Lecce, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fasciani, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Scrosati, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hassoun, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Gel–Polymer Sn–C/LiMn<sub>0.5</sub>Fe<sub>0.5</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> Battery Using a Fluorine-Free Salt</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>7</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">21198</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">21207</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.5b05179</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D7%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D21198-21207%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DD.%2BDi%2BLecce%26author%3DC.%2BFasciani%26author%3DB.%2BScrosati%26author%3DJ.%2BHassoun%26title%3DA%2BGel%25E2%2580%2593Polymer%2BSn%25E2%2580%2593C%252FLiMn0.5Fe0.5PO4%2BBattery%2BUsing%2Ba%2BFluorine-Free%2BSalt%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.5b05179&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b02768&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.5b05179&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Gel-Polymer Sn-C/LiMn0.5Fe0.5PO4 Battery Using a Fluorine-Free Salt</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Di Lecce, Daniele; Fasciani, Chiara; Scrosati, Bruno; Hassoun, Jusef</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">21198-21207</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Safety and environmental issues, because of the contemporary use of common liq. electrolytes, fluorinated salts, and LiCoO2-based cathodes in com. Li-ion batteries, might be efficiently mitigated by employing alternative gel-polymer battery configurations and new electrode materials.  Herein we study a lithium-ion polymer cell formed by combining a LiMn0.5Fe0.5PO4 olivine cathode, prepd. by simple solvothermal pathway, a nanostructured Sn-C anode, and a LiBOB-contg. PVdF-based gel electrolyte.  The polymer electrolyte, here analyzed in terms of electrochem. stability by impedance spectroscopy (EIS) and voltammetry, reveals full compatibility for cell application.  The LiBOB electrolyte salt and the electrochem. delithiaded Mn0.5Fe0.5PO4 have a higher thermal stability compared to conventional LiPF6 and Li0.5CoO2, as confirmed by thermogravimetric anal. (TGA) and by galvanostatic cycling at high temp.  LiMn0.5Fe0.5PO4 and Sn-C, showing in lithium half-cell a capacity of about 120 and 350 mAh g-1, resp., within the gelled electrolyte configuration are combined in a full Li-ion polymer battery delivering a stable capacity of about 110 mAh g-1, with working voltage ranging from 2.8 to 3.6 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrU4P4U94z9gbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljuQbfCid4Opg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVKls7zO&amp;md5=837ed24696c7b91b8081a1df7f8a37c7</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8f66dc46b325-SJC">window.refViewer={'ref1':['cit1'],'ref2':['cit2'],'ref3':['cit3'],'ref4':['cit4'],'ref5':['cit5'],'ref6':['cit6'],'ref7':['cit7'],'ref8':['cit8'],'ref9':['cit9'],'ref10':['cit10'],'ref11':['cit11'],'ref12':['cit12'],'ref13':['cit13'],'ref14':['cit14'],'ref15':['cit15'],'ref16':['cit16'],'ref17':['cit17'],'ref18':['cit18'],'ref19':['cit19'],'ref20':['cit20'],'ref21':['cit21'],'ref22':['cit22'],'ref23':['cit23'],'ref24':['cit24'],'ref25':['cit25'],'ref26':['cit26'],'ref27':['cit27'],'ref28':['cit28'],'ref29':['cit29'],'ref30':['cit30'],'ref31':['cit31'],'ref32':['cit32'],'ref33':['cit33'],'ref34':['cit34'],'ref35':['cit35'],'ref36':['cit36'],'ref37':['cit37'],'ref38':['cit38'],'ref39':['cit39'],'ref40':['cit40'],'ref41':['cit41'],'ref42':['cit42'],'ref43':['cit43'],'ref44':['cit44'],'ref45':['cit45'],'ref46':['cit46'],'ref47':['cit47']}</script><div class="articleCitedByDropzone" data-pb-dropzone="articleCitedByDropzone"><div class="cited-by"><div class="article_content-header cited-content_header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div tabindex="0" class="article_content-title"><h2 id="citeThis">Cited By</h2><div class="article__copy"> <button class="article__copy__btn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><div class="cited-by__content"><div class="sciteMetricsDropzone">

                10.1126/science.1212741</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrical Energy Storage for the Grid: A Battery of Choices</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dunn, Bruce; Kamath, Haresh; Tarascon, Jean-Marie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">334</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6058</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">928-935</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SCIEAS</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0036-8075</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The increasing interest in energy storage for the grid can be attributed to multiple factors, including the capital costs of managing peak demands, the investments needed for grid reliability, and the integration of renewable energy sources.  Although existing energy storage is dominated by pumped hydroelec., there is the recognition that battery systems can offer a no. of high-value opportunities, provided that lower costs can be obtained.  The battery systems reviewed here include sodium-sulfur batteries that are com. available for grid applications, redox-flow batteries that offer low cost, and lithium-ion batteries whose development for com. electronics and elec. vehicles is being applied to grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrZwDymuubZm7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljzNC27ihEabw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXhsVGktL%252FJ&amp;md5=5035bfda7631ad9d075e8836e61146ef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201410376"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kundu, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Talaie, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duffort, V.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nazar, L. F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Emerging Chemistry of Sodium Ion Batteries for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-ion capacitors (LICs) are hybrid energy storage devices that have the potential to bridge the gap between conventional high-energy lithium-ion batteries and high-power capacitors by combining their complementary features.  The challenge for LICs was to improve the energy storage at high charge-discharge rates by circumventing the discrepancy in kinetics between the intercalation anode and capacitive cathode.  The rational design of new nanostructured LIC electrodes that both exhibit a dominating capacitive mechanism (both double layer and pseudocapacitive) with a diminished intercalation process, is reported.  Specifically, the electrodes are a 3-dimensional interconnected TiC nanoparticle chain anode, synthesized by carbothermal conversion of graphene/TiO2 hybrid aerogels, and a pyridine-derived hierarchical porous nitrogen-doped carbon (PHPNC) cathode.  Electrochem. properties of both electrodes are thoroughly characterized which demonstrate their outstanding high-rate capabilities.  The fully assembled PHPNC//TiC LIC device delivers an energy d. of 101.5 Wh/kg and a power d. of 67.5 kW/kg (achieved at 23.4 Wh/kg), and a reasonably good cycle stability (≈82% retention after 5000 cycles) within the voltage range of 0.0-4.5 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoMyLfEXsVVTLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Ta8X0ndE3A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xjs1ejt78%253D&amp;md5=84636d13db8d9d26033becb2b5edb0e2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, H.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, L.-Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, R.-S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Development of Lithium-Sulfur Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Ta8X0ndE3A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c1ee01782a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ong, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Voltage, stability and diffusion barrier differences between sodium-ion and lithium-ion intercalation materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ong, Shyue Ping; Chevrier, Vincent L.; Hautier, Geoffroy; Jain, Anubhav; Moore, Charles; Kim, Sangtae; Ma, Xiaohua; Ceder, Gerbrand</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">To evaluate the potential of Na-ion batteries, we contrast in this work the difference between Na-ion and Li-ion based intercalation chemistries in terms of three key battery properties-voltage, phase stability and diffusion barriers.  The compds. investigated comprise the layered AMO2 and AMS2 structures, the olivine and maricite AMPO4 structures, and the NASICON A3V2(PO4)3 structures.  The calcd. Na voltages for the compds. investigated are 0.18-0.57 V lower than that of the corresponding Li voltages, in agreement with previous exptl. data.  We believe the obsd. lower voltages for Na compds. are predominantly a cathodic effect related to the much smaller energy gain from inserting Na into the host structure compared to inserting Li.  We also found a relatively strong dependence of battery properties on structural features.  In general, the difference between the Na and Li voltage of the same structure, ΔVNa-Li, is less neg. for the maricite structures preferred by Na, and more neg. for the olivine structures preferred by Li.  The layered compds. have the most neg. ΔVNa-Li.  In terms of phase stability, we found that open structures, such as the layered and NASICON structures, that are better able to accommodate the larger Na+ ion generally have both Na and Li versions of the same compd.  For the close-packed AMPO4 structures, our results show that Na generally prefers the maricite structure, while Li prefers the olivine structure, in agreement with previous exptl. work.  We also found surprising evidence that the barriers for Na+ migration can potentially be lower than that for Li+ migration in the layered structures.  Overall, our findings indicate that Na-ion systems can be competitive with Li-ion systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGosFyTQ7K1B3LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6Ta8X0ndE3A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXht1CqsLzK&amp;md5=5a6e72a3ae5ebf92d84322240b2c29cc</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1021/cr500192f"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yabuuchi, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dahbi, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Research Development on Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         rightTab-cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizUhYWWO04zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref11" class="rightTabRefNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit11" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201702093"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chao, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A sustainable iron-based sodium ion battery of porous carbon-Fe3O4/Na2FeP2O7 with high performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ming, Jun; Ming, Hai; Yang, Wenjing; Kwak, Won-Jin; Park, Jin-Bum; Zheng, Junwei; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A type of porous carbon-Fe3O4 (e.g., PC-Fe3O4) composite with an industrially scalable prodn. was introduced in the sodium ion battery application for the first time.  The PC-Fe3O4 composite, consisting of highly dispersed Fe3O4 nanocrystals within the porous carbon with a relatively low wt. percent of 45.5 wt%, could efficiently demonstrate high capacities of 225, 168, 127, 103, 98 and 90 mA h g-1 under the current densities of 50, 100, 200, 300, 400 and 500 mA g-1 with a good stability over 400 cycles.  The utilization co-efficient of Fe3O4 nanocrystals was proven to be much higher than most of the Fe3O4 nanoparticles reported recently via the study of the capacity contribution of carbon originally.  In addn., the robustness of electrode during the charge-discharge was well characterized by ex situ XRD and emission SEM (SEM).  More importantly, a new concept of an elemental iron-based sodium ion battery of PC-Fe3O4/Na2FeP2O7 is presented.  This is the first example to introduce an element-rich configuration in the sodium ion battery from the viewpoint of sustainability.  The full battery demonstrated a superior capacity of 93 mA h g-1, high capacity retention of 93.3% over 100 cycles and work voltage around 2.28 V with the energy d. of 203 W h kg-1.  Such configuration of an iron-based sodium battery would be highly promising and sustainable owing to its low cost and high stability in grid storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqlfLDULELEl7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizUhYWWO04zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXitFehtb7J&amp;md5=dbdb474ad5240a7412c37b8740147f9c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600467"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Park, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Goodenough, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene incorporation should be one effective strategy to develop advanced electrode materials for a sodium-ion battery (SIB).  Herein, the micro/nanostructural Sb/graphene composite (Sb-O-G) is successfully prepd. with the uniform Sb nanospheres (∼100 nm) bound on the graphene via oxygen bonds.  It is revealed that the in-situ-constructed oxygen bonds play a significant role on enhancing Na-storage properties, esp. the ultrafast charge/discharge capability.  The oxygen-bond-enhanced Sb-O-G composite can deliver a high capacity of 220 mAh/g at an ultrahigh c.d. of 12 A/g, which is obviously superior to the similar Sb/G composite (130 mAh/g at 10 A/g) just without Sb-O-C bonds.  It also exhibits the highest Na-storage capacity compared to Sb/G and pure Sb nanoparticles as well as the best cycling performance.  More importantly, this Sb-O-G anode achieves ultrafast (120 C) energy storage in SIB full cells, which have already been shown to power a 26-bulb array and calculator.  All of these superior performances originate from the structural stability of Sb-O-C bonds during Na uptake/release, which has been verified by ex situ X-ray photoelectron spectroscopies and IR spectroscopies.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqAWqDAYuZl6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lizUhYWWO04zA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvFylur8%253D&amp;md5=20ff4444ec296955ad0cbb06a02dfbef</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref16" class="rightTabRefNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit16" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201505943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kopold, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A rather general strategy to prep. self-supported interpenetrating 3D tricontinuous cathodes that is based on the facile electrostatic spray deposition (ESD) technique is proposed.  Taking Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) as a model system, interconnected 3D tricontinuous NVP:rGO-CNT (reduced graphene oxide-carbon nanotube) is directly deposited on the current collector without any conductive additives or binders usually needed for battery assembling.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. properties of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanograins having different carbon contents were investigated by a one-step solid state reaction and evaluated in different electrolyte systems.  It was found that the sodium storage performance in terms of capacity, coulombic efficiency and cyclability can be significantly improved in a new sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl) imide/propylene carbonate electrolyte which is introduced for the first time, bringing this material close to viability as a promising cathode for room-temp. sodium-ion batteries.  The mechanism of sodium insertion/extn. into/from Na3V2(PO4)3 lattice is analyzed by in-situ XRD technique.  The electrochem. performance of Na3V2(PO4)3 nanograins in three carbon architectures in sodium half cells were compared, demonstrating that Na3V2(PO4)3 dispersed in the acetylene carbon nanospheres has the best sodium ion battery performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoNJNGnrbWSjbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw8E4EbOk0vg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXktlSgs7s%253D&amp;md5=845e28c9f388b6524b54b10a45eb79d1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref18" class="rightTabRefNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit18" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201701968"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.-P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Y.-G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Energy/Power and Low-Temperature Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries: In Situ XRD Study and Superior Full-Cell Performance</span>. <i>Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In virtue of the abundant sodium resources, sodium ion batteries (SIBs) have been considered to be one of the promising alternatives to lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, current research concs. mostly on sodium ion half-cells, and the development of sodium ion full cells with high performance remains a crit. challenge.  Here we rationally designed a full sodium-ion battery based on nanostructured Na2Ti3O7 and VOPO4 materials as the anodes and cathodes, owing to their advantageous electrochem. features.  The full cell outputs one of the highest operating voltages close to 2.9 V and delivers a large reversible capacity of 114 mA h g-1 at a rate of 0.1C.  It also shows outstanding rate capability (∼74 mA h g-1 at 2C rate) and excellent cycling stability (92.4% capacity retention after 100 cycles).  A high energy d. of 220 W h kg-1 is achieved, which is comparable to the state-of-the-art LIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries are a very promising alternative to lithium-ion batteries because of their reliance on an abundant supply of sodium salts, environmental benignity, and low cost.  However, the low rate capability and poor long-term stability still hinder their practical application.  A cathode material, formed of RuO2-coated Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanowires, has a 50 nm diam. with the space group of I4/mmm.  When used as a cathode material for Na-ion batteries, a reversible capacity of 120 mAh g-1 at 1 C and 95 mAh g-1 at 20 C can be achieved after 1000 charge-discharge cycles.  The ultrahigh rate capability and enhanced cycling stability are comparable with high performance lithium cathodes.  Combining first principles computational investigation with exptl. observations, the excellent performance can be attributed to the uniform and highly conductive RuO2 coating and the preferred growth of the (002) plane in the Na3V2O2(PO4)2F nanowires.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqy8Uys_JBRc7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljw8E4EbOk0vg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmt1Sgtrw%253D&amp;md5=387cfec2625d5a109f637ff63f2938f1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1039/c7ee00524e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Che, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, X.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, Z.-F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrolyte Design Strategies and Research Progress for Room-temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electrolyte design or functional development is very effective at promoting the performance of sodium-ion batteries, which are attractive for electrochem. energy storage devices due to abundant sodium resources and low cost.  This review discusses recent advances on electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries and comprehensive electrolyte design strategies for various materials systems as well as functional applications.  The discussion is divided into three electrolyte types: liq., solid state, and gel state.  Liq. electrolytes are further divided into different solvent types, including org. carbonate ester, ether, ionic liq., and water.  Solid-state electrolytes also contain two types: solid polymer and glass-ceramic composite.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrochem. energy storage is one of the main societal challenges of this century.  The performances of classical lithium-ion technol. based on liq. electrolytes have made great advances in the past two decades, but the intrinsic instability of liq. electrolytes results in safety issues.  Solid polymer electrolytes would be a perfect soln. to those safety issues, miniaturization and enhancement of energy d.  However, as in liqs., the fraction of charge carried by lithium ions is small (&lt;20%), limiting the power performances.  Solid polymer electrolytes operate at 80 °C, resulting in poor mech. properties and a limited electrochem. stability window.  Here we describe a multifunctional single-ion polymer electrolyte based on polyanionic block copolymers comprising polystyrene segments.  It overcomes most of the above limitations, with a lithium-ion transport no. close to unity, excellent mech. properties and an electrochem. stability window spanning 5 V vs. Li+/Li.
